                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          <iframe data-src="https://movies.yahoo.com/video/amazing-spiderman-2-trailer-020209940.html?format=embed&amp;player_autoplay=false" data-yom-embed-source="{media_id_1:517cdb15-071c-3bbe-9d83-ebdc2f8a69cc}" frameborder="0" height="354" width="630">
                          </iframe>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          So the wallcrawler's latest enemy was born of  electric eels?
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Sony has unveiled a pretty sweet extended look at the film that kicks off (or, rather, "swings in") the 2014 summer movie season: "
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:4f53af7e-794b-33c7-8481-95d525a6d0e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://movies.yahoo.com/movie/the-amazing-spiderman-2/" target="_blank">
                           The Amazing Spider-Man 2
                          </a>
                          ," which looks to make director Marc Webb's Spidey reboot into its own entity rather than something to be constantly compared to Sam Raimi's original trilogy, which so far has had its comparative installments released exactly ten years prior to that of the new series.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Having new-to-the-big-screen Electro as what appears to be the "main villain" of "The Amazing Spider-Man 2" goes a long way in having this new Spidey establish its own identity, and the extended look sheds some (electrical) light on where this guy comes from.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The extended look opens on a (very welcome) light note with a seemingly ad-libbed argument between Peter and Aunt May regarding Peter's knack for turning everything in the laundry red and blue. We also get to see Peter genuinely enjoying being Spider-Man, particularly in a sequence in which he rescues Oscorp employee Max Dillon (Jamie Foxx).
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          From there, we see where Dillon's alter ego comes from, a villain born of Dillon wanting to "be like" Spider-Man and experimenting with high voltage  and falling into a tank of electric eels (in the same Oscorp animal testing laboratory that gave Peter Parker his powers). Geez, who lets these future bad guys into labs after-hours, anyway?
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Sony's extended look at the sequel came hot on the heels of tonight's Super Bowl spot for the film, which added further fuel to our theory that Gwen Stacy might not live to see the closing credits of "The Amazing Spider-Man 2."
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          We
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:4f53af7e-794b-33c7-8481-95d525a6d0e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://movies.yahoo.com/blogs/movie-talk/amazing-spider-man-2-spoiler-alert-emma-stone-181819870.html" target="_blank">
                           pointed out last summer
                          </a>
                          that Peter Parker's ladyfriend might be killed off in the sequel, based on set pics revealing Emma Stone in an outfit that looks like the one her comic book counterpart was wearing when she fell (and we do mean 'fell') victim to the villainy of the Green Goblin: a purple skirt, green overcoat and black boots.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Funeral clothes if there ever were any.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The Super Bowl spot wasted no time in following through on our suspicions, as the very first image had poor Gwen falling from a very great height  with a look on her face that suggests Spidey might not be able to do anything to alter her fate.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          The sequence would appear to be drawing from "The Amazing Spider-Man" #121 (June 1973), in which the Green Goblin discovers Spider-Man's true identity and kidnaps Gwen. When the Goblin throws her off the George Washington Bridge, Spidey catches her leg with a string of web but later discovers that she's dead.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Sheesh. Remember when summer movies used to be "fun"?
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Whether Sony actually wants to let go of Gwen (and Emma Stone) this early in the game remains to be seen, but most of the rest of the Super Bowl spot maintained the grim tone as Chris Cooper's Norman Osborn growls "We have plans for you" and Jamie Foxx's Electro exclaims "Let's go catch us a spider." There was a glimpse of a URL: "
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:4f53af7e-794b-33c7-8481-95d525a6d0e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://enemiesunite.com" target="_blank">
                           EnemiesUnite.com
                          </a>
                          ," which implies the triple threat of Electro, the Goblin (whose identity still isn't revealed, though we expect it's Dane DeHaan's Harry Osborn) and Paul Giamatti's Rhino is just one half of an upcoming Sinister Six supervillain team-up.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          It wasn't all doom and gloom, though  the Big Game ad closed with a bedridden Peter Parker (Andrew Garfield) claiming to Aunt May that the dirt on his face came from his attempt to clean the chimney, a sequence also featured in the extended look. Everyone knows Forest Hills, Queens isn't known for its chimneys, so  nice try, Peter.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          We have to admit  this looks good. Much, much better than the decent though frustratingly vanilla and by-the-numbers first installment in this rebooted Spidey universe.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          "
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:4f53af7e-794b-33c7-8481-95d525a6d0e0;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://movies.yahoo.com/movie/the-amazing-spiderman-2/" target="_blank">
                           The Amazing Spider-Man 2
                          </a>
                          " opens May 2.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           Watch all the movie ads from Super Bowl XLVIII:
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          <iframe data-src="https://movies.yahoo.com/video/playlist/big-game-ads---movies/?format=embed&amp;show_carousel=true&amp;player_autoplay=false" frameborder="0" height="495" width="634">
                          </iframe>
                         </p>
                        </div>

Turns 25: How That Sexy Pottery Scene Became One of the Most Romantic Movie Moments Ever","summary":"Who knew clay could be so sexy?","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F7c94d9fa0d7f8ce22548b4143f21bad997526bf3.jpg\" alt=\"&apos;Ghost&apos; Turns 25: How That Sexy Pottery Scene Became One of the Most Romantic Movie Moments Ever\" width=\"540\" height=\"371\"\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDemi Moore and Patrick Swayze make some pottery (Everett)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the middle of the night, a woman sits alone at a pottery wheel. A vintage jukebox in her apartment switches records, and &#x201C;Unchained Melody&#x201D; by the Righteous Brothers pours into the room. Her boyfriend, shirtless, approaches, sits behind her, and reaches out his hand, accidentally ruining her pot. No matter &#x2014; they begin a new one together, his hands interlaced with hers, stroking the wet clay. He begins kissing her, and she leaps into his arms, the pottery wheel abandoned in the heat of passion. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESure, it sounds ridiculous on the page &#x2014; but on the big screen in 1990, with Demi Moore and Patrick Swayze as the clay-spattered couple, it was pure magic.\u003Cb\u003E \u003C\u002Fb\u003EThis is the scene everyone thinks of when they think of \u003Ci\u003EGhost, \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ethe supernatural romance that opened in theaters 25 years ago this week. The film starred Moore as artist Molly and Swayze as her banker boyfriend Sam, who dies at the hands of a mugger and must find a way to communicate with Molly from beyond the grave. The pottery scene takes place early in the film, before his death, and it shows the audience everything we need to know about the passion between these two people. Like most great movie moments, the scene came about through a combination of hard work and happy accidents. &#x201C;We had no idea that was going to turn into the most famous love scene in history,&#x201D; Patrick Swayze said in a \u003Ci\u003EGhost \u003C\u002Fi\u003EDVD featurette. &#x201C;We were just actors trying to do the best job in the world.&#x201C; Here&#x2019;s a brief history of the scene that made millions of people consider, just for a moment, taking up pottery as a hobby.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWatch the pottery scene from&#xA0;&#x2018;Ghost.&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-embed tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Ciframe width=\"540\" height=\"404\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FCXfxUVjHFl0?feature=oembed\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhen screenwriter Bruce Joel Rubin first conceived of the character of Molly, he wrote her as a wood sculptor \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.moma.org\u002Fcollection\u002Fworks\u002F81851\"\u003Ein the vein of &#x2018;60s artist Marisol\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;I envisioned her with these big blocks of wood and with big hammers and really going at it and really powerful,&#x201D; Rubin recalled in a DVD featurette about the scene. But director Jerry Zucker worried that the idea was &#x201C;a clich&#xE9;.&#x201D; During a scoring session for his 1988 comedy \u003Ci\u003EThe Naked Gun, \u003C\u002Fi\u003EZucker noticed one of the sound editors reading a pottery magazine and had the revelation that Molly should work with clay. Rubin liked the idea, and since his wife was a potter, he had no trouble with the rewrite. (Little did he suspect, however, that he was bringing a lifetime&#x2019;s worth of dirty jokes on himself. &#x201C;Now when people come over to my house and see the pottery studio, they wink at me, &#x2018;Oh, now we know what you do at night,&#x2019;&#x201D; Rubin told \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Farticles.chicagotribune.com\u002F1991-10-24\u002Ffeatures\u002F9104050804_1_bruce-joel-rubin-ghost-script\"\u003Ethe \u003Ci\u003EChicago Tribune\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in 1991.) Molly became a clay artist, and the pottery scene emerged. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETo prepare for her role, Moore took a few pot-throwing lessons. &#x201C;I just didn&#x2019;t want my pot to wobble,&#x201D; she said in a \u003Ci\u003EGhost \u003C\u002Fi\u003Efeaturette. &#x201C;It was like a sure-fire sign that I was no good, and I was faking it.&#x201D; Swayze didn&#x2019;t receive any formal training, but he did sit at the wheel to rehearse the scene with Moore &#x2014; which was when Zucker got his first inkling of how hot the finished scene could be. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When we did the rehearsal, I just remember that it was sexy enough that it embarrassed Patrick and Demi a little bit when they were doing it,&#x201D; Zucker said on the \u003Ci\u003EGhost\u003C\u002Fi\u003E DVD commentary. &#x201C;They both had all their clothes on&#x2026; but it was still&#x2026; even then, there was something about it that was sensual.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn the day of shooting, the two actors and a small crew filmed on a closed set. Professional potters were on hand, and they started some of the pots in the scene, which Moore then completed on camera. But working with the pottery wheel proved challenging from a technical standpoint. &#x201C;There&#x2019;s a lot of footage of things flopping and spattering,&#x201D; Zucker admitted. Production designer Jane Musky recalled the challenge of achieving &#x201C;that wetness, so it was sensual, but not that it splattered all over their faces.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESwayze claimed that he didn&#x2019;t mind the mess. In Wendy Leigh&#x2019;s biography \u003Ci\u003EPatrick Swayze: One Last Dance, \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ehe&#x2019;s quoted as saying, &quot;Getting all that mud stuff all over my arms &#x2014; that was pretty sexy. Definitely got my juices going.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAt the same time, Swayze has admitted that he finds shooting love scenes extremely nerve-wracking. &#x201C;I always felt extra pressure, since I was supposed to be Mr. Sexy, if you believed all the magazines,&#x201D; Swayze wrote in his \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FThe-Time-Life-Patrick-Swayze\u002Fdp\u002F1439158614\"\u003Eautobiography \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FThe-Time-Life-Patrick-Swayze\u002Fdp\u002F1439158614\"\u003ETime of My Life\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#x201C;Of all the scenes I ever shot, I probably felt least confident about the love scenes. So it&#x2019;s ironic that the clip of Demi and me at the pottery wheel is one of the best known of my whole career.&#x201D; In Leigh&#x2019;s biography, she reveals that Swayze rehearsed the \u003Ci\u003EGhost\u003C\u002Fi\u003E scene with his wife Lisa Niemi in order to get past his embarrassment. Even so, Demi Moore claimed that &quot;Patrick&#x2019;s face turned bright red when we would even talk about the [love] scene.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMoore, too, felt awkward during filming &#x2014; particularly when the pottery scene transitioned into a full-on make-out session. In \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.people.com\u002Fpeople\u002Farchive\u002Farticle\u002F0,,20063352,00.html\"\u003Ea 1991 \u003Ci\u003EPeople \u003C\u002Fi\u003Einterview\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, she said that doing the scene with Swayze &quot;felt like we were in high school on a first date. And here we had to act like we had known each other and were comfortable with each other. We were all arms. His face was so beet red! I would say, &#x2018;Please don&#x2019;t let my breast be exposed.&#x2019; And he would say, &apos;Okay.&#x2019; If he noticed my shirt coming up over my rear, he would pull it down. We finally just said, &apos;I&#x2019;m really nervous and I hate this.&#x2019; Then it was okay.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"354\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fa9d8c71b0c83fb92b775bdaabcfbc4c1c9488902.jpg\"\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E&#x2018;Ghost&#x2019;&#xA0;(Everett)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd yet, it was clear to everyone present that Swayze and Moore were magic onscreen. One of the scene&#x2019;s most endearing moments &#x2014; when Swayze reaches over to help with the pot and accidentally collapses it &#x2014; was unplanned. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Nobody expected [the pot] to fall,&#x201D; said Rubin. &#x201C;Demi recovered so quickly&#x2026;. She wasn&#x2019;t angry, she wasn&#x2019;t disappointed. In a way, the whole nature of their relationship was shown in that moment.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe heat of the make-out scene was also more intense than anyone anticipated. &#x201C;It was one of those times in both of our careers when something happened and both of us came alive,&#x201D; said Swayze. &#xA0;Wrote the star in his autobiography: &#x201C;Demi was really good in these situations. She was very warm &#x2014; much warmer than she&#x2019;d been in the other scenes we shot together. She showed a vulnerability that was very attractive, and that really came through onscreen.&#x201D; The footage was so sensuous that, after seeing the dailies, Zucker decided not to shoot a more explicit sex scene that was in the script. (During the same sequence, Molly and Sam were supposed to make love under a sheet that covered one of Molly&#x2019;s sculptures.) &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis decision to cut the extended scene led to a continuity error that fans point out to this day: Between the pottery wheel and the groping session, the couple&#x2019;s clay-covered hands become magically clean. On the DVD commentary, Zucker is unapologetic. &#x201C;I just assumed that it was a time cut, that they didn&#x2019;t get up right from the machine and go right to this,&#x201D; he said. Then he added, &#x201C;Actually, I just didn&#x2019;t assume anything. I just wanted their hands to be not all full of clay.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe other key element to the pottery scene, of course, is the song &#x2014; a contribution from producer Lisa Weinstein, who brought Zucker a cassette tape of &#x201C;Unchained Melody&#x201D; during filming. &#x201C;The longing of that music, the pain of the music is wonderful,&#x201D; said Zucker. Coincidentally, Righteous Brothers singer Bill Medley also sang &#x201C;Time of My Life,&#x201D; the theme song from Swayze&#x2019;s biggest hit before \u003Ci\u003EGhost\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, 1987&#x2019;s\u003Ci\u003E Dirty Dancing. \u003C\u002Fi\u003E&#x201C;I think we&#x2019;re gonna have to do a duet soon or something,&#x201D; Swayze joked in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=ENGEOIj9h3A&amp;feature=youtu.be&amp;t=1m6s\"\u003Ea 1990 interview\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMedley himself received a major career boost from \u003Ci\u003EGhost. \u003C\u002Fi\u003EWritten for the forgotten 1955 prison film \u003Ci\u003EUnchained \u003C\u002Fi\u003E(hence the title) and recorded by the Righteous Brothers in 1965, &#x201C;Unchained Melody&#x201D; became a resurgent hit in 1990, climbing to No. 19 on the Billboard Hot 100. Even more impressive: It made Medley cool again. &#x201C;My kids were about nine and ten at the time, and all of a sudden I became the hero of the neighborhood,&#x201D; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.rollingstone.com\u002Fmusic\u002Fnews\u002Frock-and-roll-hall-of-fame-the-righteous-brothers-20030228#ixzz3fVOOPTD2\"\u003Ehe told \u003Ci\u003ERolling Stone\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in 2003\u003Ci\u003E. \u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.boxofficemojo.com\u002Fyearly\u002Fchart\u002F?view2=worldwide&amp;yr=1990\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EGhost \u003C\u002Fi\u003Ewas a massive hit\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; the highest-grossing film globally of 1990, besting \u003Ci\u003EHome Alone\u003C\u002Fi\u003E and \u003Ci\u003EPretty Woman\u003C\u002Fi\u003E &#x2014; and the pottery scene became instantly iconic. Pop culture has since become cluttered with parodies and homages; faux-sensuous pot-throwing scenes have been featured in the film \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=1_LfUmdR2Mo\"\u003ENaked Gun 2 &#xBD; \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E(directed by Jerry Zucker&#x2019;s brother David), and on \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=fGnzhTvQqaA\"\u003EFamily Guy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=b1rErLucpb4\"\u003EGlee\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=VqBoDDfXWZ4\"\u003ETwo and a Half Men\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=_L0xl7s4wAg\"\u003ECommunity\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eand \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=S4gW7veUPDg\"\u003ELate Night with Jimmy Fallon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eto name a few. An Iowa reporter made headlines two years ago when he \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=JRdLS-WxXEo\"\u003Espoofed the scene during a live interview\u003C\u002Fa\u003E at a Cedar Rapids ceramics studio. Swayze and Moore&#x2019;s scene is frequently cited as one of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nydailynews.com\u002Fentertainment\u002Fmovies\u002F50-sexiest-movie-scenes-article-1.2114249\"\u003Esexiest\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theguardian.com\u002Fuk\u002F2003\u002Ffeb\u002F07\u002Fvalentinesday2003.film\"\u003Emost romantic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E film moments of all time.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E
